
   Message Format
  ----------------

   Message #1 of 8212 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

   <Subject>

   <1 blank separator line>

   <Date/Time>

   <Person & email address>

   <2 blank separator lines then...>

   <Message - "As-Is">

   <2 blank lines then @'s as divider line>


   * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
     Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
     is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
     view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
     Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
     "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

     Thanks to Mark de Jong (from the AMOS-LIST) for helping me with rebuilding
     Floquet's ASCII signiture. (who else would keep emails for 7 years?!)

     Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
     me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

     Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
     the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
     addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.


   Message From Archivist
  ------------------------

   I hope everyone enjoys reading the messages and appreciates me archiving
   them. It took hours of work to get all the info into this file and then 
   rebuild the ASCII signitures as best as I could.
   Don't forget to join, or atleast visit, the Y! AMOS-LIST group:

     http://groups.yahoo.com/group/amos-list


          - Andrew D. Burton, January 2008
            aliensrcooluk@yahoo.co.uk 
            http://www.geocities.com/aliensrcooluk

	Message #1227 of 8199

Re: Wanted

Thu Oct 1, 1998 7:01 pm
"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


Normally I avoid these kind of threads but for some reason today I
just can hold back...

> Amos is not the best. It is just the best for begginning in all
> purposes... Do you remember what "B.A.S.I.C." means ?
> It stays anyway a very good language.

> I don't agree! AMOS provides very easy programming with full
> (almost) acces to Amiga's capabilities. Can anyone suggest an alternative?

I'm with you on this one, look the things that amos is good at (2D
scrolling, Sprites/Bobs, Screen Handling, ect. ect.) are percisely the
thing the Amiga is good at, whereas the things Amos is bad for (maths, 3D
texture mapping/Ray casting, scaling ect.) are percisely the things the
Amiga is bad at. And just to be really annoying, I don't think Amos is
the best language to learn on, PASCAL is really (it has no GOTO command!)
Amos is good to use but it'll let you get away with too much sloppy code
to be a good beginer's language. Maybe I'm misstepping here, but it seems
the oldest, wisest folks on the list are those who've had experience
beyond Amos, I know I never wrote a decent piece of code until my first
"Hello World" in C, but still I always come back to Amos when I want to do
something serious, why? Because it's the best, fastest way to turn an
Idea in your head into a game on your screen. That is just so long as
your idea isn't for a 3-D guradu shaded texture mapped wonderland.

scott matott sXe

Exactly! I've had this arguement with my friend several times! I wanted a
program to change all my MAME Roms (over 85!) that were in directories into
ZIP files. In less than 5 minutes with AMOS (plus the AMCAF extension) I
had a program up and running! I didn't have to learn how to use libraries
to make a file tree..blah blah blah. Sorry, I'm just too lazy to learn how
to do all that! :)

Okay you have obviously not used amos outside of amos!
The good thing about amos is it allows use of assembler and doscalls and so
on... so it isn't just BASIC! its much more... I mean you compare Qbasic and
AmosPro they are totally different! And as for PASCAL! Ha! I admit i have
only learnt the basics and a little extra.. but it is no where near as good
as Amos... Okay it may be good that you have to setup everything and i don't
know about wether amos is faster or not! But so far the only good thing to
do with Pascal that i have found is its variable structure using TYPE! But I
don't think AMOS is just a starting language... its a good starting language
but its a middling language too = ) ! I do agree though that the more
experience with other languages you have the better! And again I agree but i
only find a problem with speed... I can do anything any other language can
do with 10* more ease but 10* less speed! Coz Amos can handle 3D and
Tmapping.. its just too slow! But with using DMA you can do alot! And thats
what i try to do with my progs. Use the lowest level I can possible do in
amos to get the most power and speed!

Re: Wanted

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as Scooter,
> > Amos is not the best. It is just the best for begginning in all
> > purposes... Do you remember what "B.A.S.I.C." means ?

We all know. Amos is so much more than that. It is probably the best
implementation of "BASIC" I have ever seen. Yeah you can get a bit
faster, or a bit more OS friendly, but you sure can't get anything
easier to develop in. Everything is already there.

> > It stays anyway a very good language.
> > I don't agree! AMOS provides very easy programming with full
> > (almost) acces to Amiga's capabilities. Can anyone suggest an alternative?

Oh yeah, there are alternatives. Loads of them. All more expensive
and a heck of a lot harder to use. Some of them you need to study
and study and study, and then use library calls to do anything with
anyway. Yuk.

> I'm with you on this one, look the things that amos is good at (2D
> scrolling, Sprites/Bobs, Screen Handling, ect. ect.) are percisely the
> thing the Amiga is good at, whereas the things Amos is bad for (maths, 3D
> texture mapping/Ray casting, scaling ect.) are percisely the things the
> Amiga is bad at. And just to be really annoying, I don't think Amos is
> the best language to learn on, PASCAL is really (it has no GOTO command!)

Note to Ghizzo: Ditch GOTO from AmosNG...

Note to "you know who you are": You can learn to live without goto ;-)

> Amos is good to use but it'll let you get away with too much sloppy code
> to be a good beginer's language. Maybe I'm misstepping here, but it seems
> the oldest, wisest folks on the list are those who've had experience
> beyond Amos, I know I never wrote a decent piece of code until my first
> "Hello World" in C, but still I always come back to Amos when I want to do
> something serious, why? Because it's the best, fastest way to turn an
> Idea in your head into a game on your screen. That is just so long as
> your idea isn't for a 3-D guradu shaded texture mapped wonderland.

;-)

Ah, yes you can't do much with PASCAL but I submit it is the best
learning language because it is forceably structured, there's no bouncing
around from here to there and back again in pascal you've got to divide
every task into it's own seperate and discrete function. Thus pascal does
what I think amos can't and that's teaches you to think about code in an
orderly and efficient way. Amos by contrast will let you get away with
anything and so it's not as good for learning structure.

> don't think AMOS is just a starting language... its a good starting language
> but its a middling language too = ) ! I do agree though that the more
> experience with other languages you have the better!
Ah then we agree anyway, I guess you're just not a fan of PASCAL
that's all. :) But I'm totally with you on AMOS as a middling language to
use your words. It is very powerful and so easy to use, maybe if you
really, really need the speed it can fail you, but if you're only making
2D old school style games (the kind the Amiga itself was designed with in
mind) it is plenty fast enough.

And again I agree but i
> only find a problem with speed... I can do anything any other language can
> do with 10* more ease but 10* less speed! Coz Amos can handle 3D and
> Tmapping.. its just too slow!
Yeah although what I was saying was that you should also consider
that the amiga itself is slown at these things, I mean the main bottle
kneck with ray casting is getting an entire new screen worth of pixels
written every 50th of a second. The amiga just isn't made to update that
much of the screen at once.

But with using DMA you can do alot! And thats
> what i try to do with my progs. Use the lowest level I can possible do in
> amos to get the most power and speed!
>
it's a good call about assembler, thus amos can be flexible, easy
when you want it and fast when you need it.

victory when at least I achieved to compile it. 8)

	Message #1253 of 8199 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: To Goto or Not To Goto...

Sat Oct 3, 1998 3:35 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>> I think GOTO can be helpful during developement, like if you wanted
>> to skip a section of code while debugging instead of trying to
>> comment it out, or make it into a Proc or Sub.
> Nope....
> Whats wrong with
> if 1=0
> 'stuff to skip...
> end if
> Sod commenting out.

Yep... or even something a bit more like C/C++ as follows...

DEBUG=True

If DEBUG=True
'stuff to skip...
End If

Of course it's actually exactly the same as your idea, Keith, but I
just like the lable as it adds a bit more clarity. You can also do
things like...

DEBUG_ONE=False
DEBUG_TWO=True
DEBUG_THREE=False
etc. etc.

IF DEBUG_ONE=True
'First section to skip...
End If

IF DEBUG_TWO=True
'Second section to skip...
End If

IF DEBUG_THREE=True
'Third section to skip...
End If

Now, simply changing the status of the DEBUGS at the top of your
program would enable/disable the execution of each section.

Again, it's really all the same principle, but kind of a new twist.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

You can't use the WB GUI with amos alone. You need to install an
extension. GUI 1.70 extention is aparently quite good, I sugest you get
a copy of that.

An extention add commands that AMOS didn't have originly or wasn't
very good at.


I'd also recomend Turbo+ extention for the fast drawing commands, I
could send it to you if you want.


There is also a 3D extention, but I wouldn't bother with that: its
not very good.

You can get that along with other 'goodies' from
http://users.cybercity.dk/~ccc21504/amos/front.html

how other people debugged their programs and thought I'd share my
approach.

C64... funny as I often used Gosub in AMOS, but then that is a more
modular-oriented command. Procedures are the way to go... and
like my friend Ben Wyatt told me many times... "You can fold them
right up"... a very addicting feature.

Re: Gui probs.?

Sun Oct 4, 1998 3:25 pm
"Rev. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


On 04-Oct-98, Stephen Thornber wrote:
>Load "Dh1:Amos/gui.abk"
>Gui Bank 20
>Amos To Back

/Gui Amiga 0/ instead

>Gui Open 1,1
>Do
> GW=Gui Wait
> If GW=-1

/A=Gui Close(1)/
/Gui Amos/
/End If/

>Loop

>Now that opens my gui very nicely, but when I click on the
>close gadget, not only does the gui close, but so does AmosPro
>and It wont re-load without a boot.?

You've sent amos to back, but never brought it back to front. Also, install
the ams command in c:. If amos locks while your gui is running, ams will take
you back to the amos environmnent.

>is there no way to keep AmosPro open as well as the gui, so
>I can modify my code.?

Yes, but you have to remember to bring amos back to front at the end. Using
Gui Amiga 0 and Gui Amos are the best bet.

I'm also sending you my gui tutorial, that will get you over the next 50
questions you are going to ask. Q8-{)

Well met and godspeed,

II class, which was supposed to give me college credit, was turned into a
"who can beat Lost Vikings the fastest" class.

was

books we had were pretty out dated, they considered the C64 a brand new
computer on the market!

I never use GOTOs for anything other than skipping over a little code while
trying to fix some code. I do not support any other use of it. :)

Re: AmosPro Newbie

Mon Oct 5, 1998 12:33 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,


> Great, how about a prog that opens a requestor and you pick a file
> then the program gives you the version info on the file you
> picked. I'd love a util to do that, but I wouldn't have a clue
> how to code it.. ??

> Steve

Writen and tested in 5 minutes flat.


The notes I've left arn't very good, but you can use online help with
commands you don't know:


(just cut that section out, save it as ver.asc, and merge it as ascii in
the amos FILE menu)

------------------------------------------------------
F$=Fsel$("")
' Opens AMOS file requester.
'
' (You can use ASL requesters with some extentions ;)


Open In 1,F$
' Opens that file for input (we won't input from it though)

L=Lof(1)
' Gets the size of the file in input

Close
' Closes that file


Reserve As Work 5,L
' Reserves the right ammount of memory to load that file

Bload F$,Start(5)
' Loads the file to the start of memory bank 5


P=0

For A=0 To L

Scan through the file with variable A

S=Start(5)


If P=0

' P is a tempory marker to show whever we've found '$VER'

P1=Peek(A+S)
P2=Peek(A+S+1)
P3=Peek(A+S+2)
P4=Peek(A+S+3)
' Reads from memory bank 5 + A at various offsets

If Chr$(P1)="$" and Chr$(P2)="V" and Chr$(P3)="E" and Chr$(P4)="R"

' Check if we find '$VER'

P=1

End If

End If
If P=1

P1=Peek(A+S)

If P1=0
End
End If
' Check for end of $VER

Print Chr$(P1);
' Print version


End If
Next
------------------------------------------------------

As for the simple demos, I'll get back to you in a day or too.

See ya.

	Message #1289 of 8199 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Goto.?

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as Stephen,
> Hi all.

Greetings newcomer, welcome.

> I've been reading all the recent mail on "goto"'s
> one thing puzzles me though.?
> What is so bad about using GOTO in your programs.?

Urk. A goto has no useful function, and can lead to very bad programming
and impossible to read programs. (Ask any cobol programmer) A goto
allows you to jump around in your code all over the place, without proper
control. A program should flow naturally, and be nice and easy to read,
amd preferably make sense (at least to the programmer) and contain proper
comments. (You know you want to...)

> (Sorry if this makes me sounds stupid or ignorant, but I'd
> like to know, why I shouldn't use them. :)

In simple terms, you don't need them. If you NEED to resort to a goto, you need
to read more manuals. ;-)

	Message #1291 of 8199 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

GOTOs

Mon Oct 5, 1998 10:51 am
"floquet" <floquet@hp-sc.univ-lille2.fr>


> From: Stephen Thornber <SThornber@steve1.demon.co.uk>
> (Sorry if this makes me sounds stupid or ignorant, but I'd
> like to know, why I shouldn't use them. :)

GOTO is an instruction unuseful and dangerous.
Unuseful because with a good program structure you don't need it. That
forces you to think about your program before you start typing.
Someting like :
AGAIN:
' some code
If _lifes>0 then goto again
Must be coded :
While _lifes>0
' some code
Wend
You naturally think "I play while I have lifes".
So your code is more "natural" and readable. In 6 monthes you still will
be able to read and understand what you write now.
Dangerous besause you can code this:
If blabla then goto SHMURTZ
' lots of code
Gosub SHMURTZ
' lots of code
SHMURTZ:
' something
Return
If the "blabla" condition is rarely true, your prog may work, until that
day where you'll get a "RETURN WITHOUT GOSUB" and hard way to find why.

That's for Amos. But in general case, avoid GOTO. I daily program at
work with a language with no goto, and I've no problem with that.

The only language that obliges you to use GOTOs is COBOL !!!

Hi Guys.

I've come across a couple of problems,
one is just annoying, the other is my main concern.

1:- (the annoying one)

I designed a simple gui (a slider and 2 buttons)
it works fine, so I added a bit of code to
print the current setting of the slider on the gui,
using "gui Text", well that works fine.. BUT

If I move the slider to a high position, the gui will
show, say errrm "12", then when I move it down to something
like "5", instead of "5", I get "52".

Its not printing over the last piece of text..
I tried several ways to fix the problem, the most obvious
one was to print " " at the same co-ords, just before
it prints the number. (to clear the last number)
but this doesn't work... now for something wierd.
If I change the " " to something like "___" or "XXX"
it works fine, overwriting the previous text..
but ___ or XXX looks ugly..
the question is... why doesn't 3 spaces work the same..?!?!

I eventually fixed it by using "gui bar" to wipe out the
text, but I'd rather use the " " method..

(sorry for the looooong text, but I couldn't explain it
any easier ;)

2:- (the main problem)

I added some code to my simple gui to iconify itself
when I clicked on a button, this works fine.
but I'd like it to uniconify when I click on the close
gadget of the iconified window. I can't get this to
work at all, in fact it won't read the close button
at all, when its iconified. and I have to use Ctrl+C.

my code is like this:-

Procedure ICONIFY
Gui Iconify 1
X=0
Repeat
GW=Gui Wait
If GW=-1
Gui Uniconify 1
X=1
EndIf
Until X=1
Endproc

Anyone tell me how to read the close gadget when my
window is iconified..?!?!

(Please forgive my sloppy code, I am learning, but
slowly... :)


Thanks in Advance :)

I must say this discussion of Goto is just what the Amos list is for, it
makes useful reading material, these are the type of mails that I save.
I have read experienced programers slagging-off Goto and have discovered the
problems with it myself, but beginners need to know these things. However,
the use of Goto to *temporarily* jump past a bit of program to test
something is very useful though, I bet most Amos coders glance over their
shoulder and do that dirty thing sometimes. (indignant outrage follows!)

Thanks, people, keep it up.

>usefull for the Demo I'm working on!

The chunky is faster for games where the full screen completely changes,
like 3D games for example, as drawing pixels is dead slow!
like just a or.w #%1010101010101010,(a0) is dead slow, as its
writing to chipmem (yuk!)
where in chunky it writes to fastmem, and the C2P will covert it into
chip mem & planar, so it does turn out faster there.
Where as for 2d games like platformers you can use the blittler to draw
but then with rtg....

I might use kalms c2p routine, as its one of the best ive seen, its used
in loads of demos and some doom ports, also Im good friends with him
so getting permission shouldnt be too hard.

>What do you mean by Dos,Int,gfx and library calls.??!?!


Amos has some internal commands that don't need any extensions or any
extralibries because they call apon the system libraries...
These commands are called
Doscal (-X) - Has control over OS
IntCall (-X) - has Control over Intuition
GfxCall (-X) - Has Control over Graphics!
-X is the Library offset! Basically a library is a store of other peoples
code... Code that is very usefull... You need to know the offset in the
library to get the right bit of code! But I wouldn't try these commands out
as a begginer they are very powerfull and basically have no saftey
precautions so if you get it wrong... you crash! And me just talking about
this will just confuse things... Unless i'm completley wrong and you are a
very quick learner... But I know when i started I tried these commands and
just though they were put there so that you would RTFM (Thankyou! for
enlightening me! = P) and find nothing on these bloody commands! But if you
want I will explain in more detail!

	Message #1304 of 8200 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: GOTOs

Mon Oct 5, 1998 10:48 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 05-Okt-98, floquet wrote:

f>> (Sorry if this makes me sounds stupid or ignorant, but I'd
f>> like to know, why I shouldn't use them. :)

f> GOTO is an instruction unuseful and dangerous.

I agree that it could be dangerous if you don't know how to use it. But I
disagree that it is unuseful.

f> Unuseful because with a good program structure you don't need it. That

One good place for using goto is exiting from nested loops. In Amos we can
Exit 2 or Exit 3 , I don't know for Pascal, but in C, there's no such
thing, and the best way to exit nested loops is to use goto.

A place where Goto could be useful in Amos is:

Procedure SOMEPROC
'a lot of init code
Do
'a lot of code
If SOMETHING
For I=WHATEVER To WHATEVER2
If SOMETHING_ELSE
Goto _EXIT
End If
Next
End If
'a lot of code
Loop
_EXIT:
'a lot of cleanup code
End Proc

Now, when you need to exit from procedure, you can't Pop Proc because that
would skip cleanup code, you can't Exit 2 because For loop is inside If
block, and you can't set some exit flag and use While instead of Do because
you have a lot of code which could do something unexpected. Even if you
could do something of that, in this case, Goto is most readable solution.

So, I would conclude, that Goto is bad, but sometimes it is neccesary :)

Regards

...Pah. See below.

Oops, forgot to skip "a lot of code"

BTW, your code forgets to dereference the next, and the if, and the other
if, and the loop. You are relying on the "end proc" to close everything
down for you. Yuk.

Procedure SOMEPROC
'a lot of init code
Do
'a lot of code
If SOMETHING
For I=WHATEVER To WHATEVER2
If SOMETHING_ELSE
i=whatever2
skip=true
End If
Next
End If
if not skip
'a lot of code
end if
Loop
'a lot of cleanup code
End Proc

Which is a horrible way of writing code, but its better than the goto, as
everythng is closed down cleanly. I have had to debug other peoples work
before, and people make such a mess.... The dominant code in your loop
is a "lot of code", rather than the use of a goto, which is a conditional
chunk, so rewrite the condition out of the loop, or seperate your loops.
Why are you putting so much in ONE procedure ? Would it be easier to
seperate them out perhaps ? Now your excercise for today is to rewrite
your loop nice and cleanly with the code to skip outside the loop.

:-P

Next goto for me to kill please..

Goto is useless.

Exactly!! Keith, have you been looking at my code again?! This is
the same method I use to break out of loops, whether they be in
BASIC, C or whatever... it is logical and safe.


> Goto is useless.

Well, I wouldn't say it is completely useless, but completely
unnecessary... hmm, I guess that sort of equals the same thing in the
end, doesn't it. haha. :)

Anyway, someone was asking about Goto and why they are advised
not to use it...
Goto is a throwback to the first programming languages, there was a
time when Goto was the ONLY command we had for passing control
around a program. As the size and complexity of programs
increased, Goto became increasingly more cumbersome to work with
and introduced what is known as Spaghetti Code, not a good thing.

A major evolution occured which was the dawn of structured
programming, definitely a good thing. These languages added
powerful contol structures such as Repeat...Until, While...Wend, etc.
all things which programmers were previously forced to implement
by relying on Goto...

Anyway, that's about the way I remember it... I can remember being
so amazed when I was first exposed to a While... Wend loop
structure and real procedures... radical stuff at that time. This was
before they were commonly accepted, but it was obvious they were
preferable to Goto!!!


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

	Message #1314 of 8200

FORTRAN Gotos

Tue Oct 6, 1998 12:35 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


Hi all,

I have to add my two cents on the GOTO debate.

I use FORTRAN at work, and it's probably the most widely used command in
our entire system. I must confess to using GOTO's regularly in my FORTRAN
code (I tried once to go without it, but it's amazing how ugly and
unreadable to code becomes (and inefficient!) when everything is
conditional). DO loops are the main culprit, as jumping out of the loop is
much better than letting the loop complete until it's end (DO loops are NOT
conditional in FORTRAN - at least not the version of FORTRAN I use).

However, in all my playing around with AMOS, I think I used a GOTO once -
and only as a simple debugging tool that I discarded once I had my problem
solved. The Conditional Loops available in AMOS are good. They make
things much easier and more "structured".

So kiddies, don't use GOTO's unless the alternative is worse or
non-existent. In AMOS, I don't really see the need at all.

Phil 8-)

p.s: For your consideration: is an Exit command just as bad as a GOTO?
(Probably not, now that I think of it, as GOTO's can go BACKWARDS... which
is what makes them REALLY bad if misused!)

Phil (-8

Re: GOTOs

Tue Oct 6, 1998 2:24 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> For my next trick, this is how to implement a looping on/off thing
> without messing about much.
> while 1
> a=1-a
> print a
> wend

Haha... and there you have it from Braneloc, The Amazing himself.

What is it with all of these numeric literals... I prefer something
like...

NOTDONE=True
While NOTDONE
A=1-A
Print A
' ...Insert conditional check for exiting loop here
Wend


>>> Goto is useless.
> Well, I suppose you could use it to scramble code, make it unreadable,
> jump all over the place and fill the stack with unreturned values,
> crash the system with an illegal call and suddenly return to the
> wrong part of the program when you finally pop the stack...

The problem is that you are going to have people saying "well, you
just don't know how to use Goto effectively... if you're really GOOD,
I mean a REALLY REALLY GOOD programmer like me then you can
use Goto without causing all of those problems!!"... haha.


> I would strongly advise putting your conditional tests at the beginning
> with while...wend as opposed to repeat...until. Trust me. You have
> a lot more control over while/wend. Repeat/until is only usefull if
> you absolutely, positively, HAVE to run a loop at LEAST once.

Not to mention that if you move to C or C++ there is no direct
replacement for Repeat...Until, but there is the same old While...
Wend structure. Of course, you can use Do...While in C/C++, but the
logic is reversed. Actually, I have always found Repeat...Until to be
quite effective in AMOS, but you do need to keep in mind that
your code will be executed a minimum of one time, as Keith has
pointed out.

And there you have it... your weekly lesson in entertainment and
good programming practice brought to you by Keith Hill, floquet and
yours truly.

Enjoy!! :-)

Lets not get into this debate again!!!

Tue Oct 6, 1998 2:27 am
"Dave Paterson" <y2guru@sprynet.com>


Dear all,

Im sick and tired of everyone bitching about how crap Blitz is in comparison to
Amos, first of all you obviously havent used blitz to come to that conclusion
and secondly you obviously havent used amos enough to know its limitations.

Blitz's strength is its compiler and integrated AGA and intution support, not to
mention messing with DMA, its biggest draw back is its documentation and its
poor editor.

Amos's strength is its easy to use editor and almost crash free environment, its
drawback is its poor performance.

All programming tools have their strengths and weaknesses, put their strengths
to good use!!!!!

END OF STORY

Dave Paterson

	Message #1328 of 8200 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: FORTRAN Gotos

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as pbrowne,
> So kiddies, don't use GOTO's unless the alternative is worse or
> non-existent. In AMOS, I don't really see the need at all.

;-)

> p.s: For your consideration: is an Exit command just as bad as a GOTO?
> (Probably not, now that I think of it, as GOTO's can go BACKWARDS... which
> is what makes them REALLY bad if misused!)

No. First there Is a concept called "the stack". Program jumps like gosub
or procedure calls put temporary variables here in a fifo format, and the
"return address" of all calls is put here. Goto bypasses this, allowing you
to jump anywhere and do anything, but does nothing with the stack, hence
all of a sudden error messages if you are not carefull. Exit uses the stack,
and pops out of the loop by artificially popping the stack and returning to
the correct point in the program.

That was a public information broadcast.

Re: GOTOs

Tue Oct 6, 1998 7:28 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 06-Okt-98, Keith Hill wrote:

KH>>> Procedure SOMEPROC
KH>>> 'a lot of init code
KH>>> Do
KH>>> 'a lot of code
KH>>> If SOMETHING
KH>>> For I=WHATEVER To WHATEVER2
KH>>> If SOMETHING_ELSE
KH>>> Goto _EXIT
KH>>> End If
KH>>> Next
KH>>> End If
KH>>> 'a lot of code
KH>>> Loop
KH>>> _EXIT:
KH>>> 'a lot of cleanup code
KH>>> End Proc

KH> ...Pah. See below.

KH> Oops, forgot to skip "a lot of code"

Yes :)

KH> BTW, your code forgets to dereference the next, and the if, and the
other
KH> if, and the loop. You are relying on the "end proc" to close
everything
KH> down for you. Yuk.

So? End Proc can do that. Tell me honest, if you were doing something like
this, and there is no need for cleanup code, wouldn't you simply Pop Proc?

KH> Procedure SOMEPROC
KH> 'a lot of init code
KH> Do
KH> 'a lot of code
KH> If SOMETHING
KH> For I=WHATEVER To WHATEVER2
KH> If SOMETHING_ELSE
KH> i=whatever2

Why do you use this instead of Exit? It doesn't skip any code you might
have below End If, and it is less obvious for what it does.

KH> skip=true

Re: GOTOs

Tue Oct 6, 1998 2:14 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


-----Original Message-----
From: Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 05 October 1998 21:10
Subject: [amos-list] Re: GOTOs


>From: Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>
>
>On 05-Okt-98, floquet wrote:
>
>f>> (Sorry if this makes me sounds stupid or ignorant, but I'd
>f>> like to know, why I shouldn't use them. :)
>
>f> GOTO is an instruction unuseful and dangerous.
>
>I agree that it could be dangerous if you don't know how to use it. But I
>disagree that it is unuseful.
>
>f> Unuseful because with a good program structure you don't need it. That
>
>One good place for using goto is exiting from nested loops. In Amos we can
>Exit 2 or Exit 3 , I don't know for Pascal, but in C, there's no such
>thing, and the best way to exit nested loops is to use goto.
>
>A place where Goto could be useful in Amos is:
>
>Procedure SOMEPROC
> 'a lot of init code
> Do
> 'a lot of code
> If SOMETHING
> For I=WHATEVER To WHATEVER2
> If SOMETHING_ELSE
> Goto _EXIT
> End If
> Next
> End If
> 'a lot of code
> Loop
> _EXIT:
> 'a lot of cleanup code
>End Proc
>
>Now, when you need to exit from procedure, you can't Pop Proc because that
>would skip cleanup code, you can't Exit 2 because For loop is inside If
>block, and you can't set some exit flag and use While instead of Do because
>you have a lot of code which could do something unexpected. Even if you
>could do something of that, in this case, Goto is most readable solution.
>
>So, I would conclude, that Goto is bad, but sometimes it is neccesary :)
>

Cool! I agree with Nikola... it can be useful I don't use it but it can
be... So now thats been sorted pehaps this argument about a simple stupid
command could stop!
I don't like the if statement but hey! Its usefull but it is quite slow! I
think Amos should have a Case statement too!

"Oh leave me alone..... I'm walkin out of the door..... Leave me alone!"

	Message #1340 of 8200 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: GOTOs

Tue Oct 6, 1998 5:39 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>>The problem is that you are going to have people saying "well, you
>>just don't know how to use Goto effectively... if you're really GOOD,
>>I mean a REALLY REALLY GOOD programmer like me then you can
>>use Goto without causing all of those problems!!"... haha.
> Are you talking about me?

Haha... no, I was speaking in general.


> Well, I'm not a really really good programmer speaking both about
> my programs and amount of theory I know (very little). But I don't
> want to be dogmatic about anything, and if I couldn't think of a good
> example for Goto, I would probably reply that there might be some
> cases where Goto is usable, but I don't know them.

Well, in a previous post I said that I don't think Goto is completely
useless, but rather it is completely unnecessary due to advances in
programming languages. It's another question whether being
unnecessary equals useless. It's all a matter of style really... of
course you could use Goto in loads of places and anyone is obviously
free to do so, but some of us are simply saying there are better ways
to handle this... for every place someone might use a Goto, we could
provide a "non-Goto" (copyright 1998 Garfield Benjamin) solution.


> Have you seen all programs in the world, so that you can tell that
> there is not a single usable Goto in them?

As a matter of fact I have... haha. Of course I have not seen every
program in the world, but then I do not need to. I have seen and
written enough programs to know there is always an elegant
solution to replace a section of code relying on Goto.

It's really a matter of preference and programming is a very personal
thing... we each have our own style to a degree and no one can say
what is right or wrong for someone else, we only know what is
right for ourselves. However, there are certain aspects of
programming which are universally true and structured programming
or object oriented programming introduced new methods which are
"better" in many ways.


> BTW, goto for exiting from nested loops is *recommended* for use in
> C by authors of C themselves. I have tried it, and I agree about that.
> BTW2, I still don't know how to exit nested loops in Pascal...

Wow, I haven't used Pascal in a long time... from what I remember,
it was a very nice language... kind of a cross between BASIC and C.

Why not simply set your loop variables to equal the EndLoop states?
Example in AMOS code ( to help us stay focused )

For REP1=1 To 10
For REP2=1 To 100
For REP3=1 To 1000
If NEEDTOEXIT
REP3=1001 : REP2=101 : REP1=11
End If
Next REP3
Next REP2
Next REP1

That's the method I use in AMOS, BLITZ, C, etc. Of course, you can
Pop out of AMOS and BLITZ's loop I believe, but I have always found
it's easier to find a good solution then stick to it... that's part of
the benefit of choosing the "right" solution... it is 100% portable
between languages.


> That logic has always confused me, and for a long time I wasnt sure
> will Repeat Until condition be looped if condition is true or false.
> Bwyatt in POP had a solution to this:
> Do While... Loop
> Do...Loop While
> Do Until... Loop
> Do... Loop Until
> You could even make combinations like:
> Do While... Loop Until
> We should convince him to continue work ;)

Haha... yes, Ben is a clever guy. Hmm... that idea about the
combination looks a bit strange, now doesn't it? We have a Do While
loop condition at the top combined with a Repeat Until condition at
the bottom... very unique. Ben what were you thinking there? Was
this simply to illustrate that the programmer has complete flexibility??

Okay, this has been interesting... talking about programming style is
always a good thing, but we better stop and get back to pure AMOS,
and I think that's where this thread began... :-)

FMV is Full Motion Video, ya know, like in the intro to psx games 8o)


>Sorry for askin somany questions i'm just curious.. as I would love to make
>my own extension... It would be to do with Maths and Graphics! And lots of
>different versions of the Copy command.. to give more control with the data
>that is being moved? I mean it would make things so much easyier..
>especially when manipulating Bitplanes to have a copy command that doesn't
>write the 0's coz then you would have a masked copy! etc. Also a Better
>Polygon command.... one that uses a proper polygontable and Flags! or maybe
>a polygon to and a poly end command coz a the moment the problem is you have
>to set the data the polygon uses at the beginning of the prog and that
>amount of sides i fixed when ever you run the prog...
>but you cant build a pollygon like this!...

To make a extension you will need:

a assembler (get phxass off aminet)
|Music.s (AMOSPro_Tutorial:Extensions/)
and thats it.

Read |Music.s, its the source for the (useless) music extension,
it has all of the extra amos functions and macro definitions and stuff.

you'll need some knowledge of assembly, |music.s
and all amos extensions are compiled with GenAm,
which is crap compared to Phxass.

Phxass does everything that GenAm does, but its much faster
at compiling, for example, it takes GenAm about 10secs to compile
TGE, and PhxAss would do it in about 2secs.

I'll help you with any probs you encounter with extension coding 8)

>Do you have any ideas how i could learn to make an extension? Docs? or
>source code? or should i just go write a 'Hello world' program coz an ext.
>is way out of my league?

I wouldnt say that, you just need to know move.l 8)
and things like shifting, swapping and stuff, its
all pretty basic, it just is harder to debug 8)
heres a tip tho that I used when coding TGE:
Dont Write Bugs.

it saves hours of time 8o)

OK, just quickly 'cause I'm supposed to be WORKING ;) , I re-read my
manual, where it states quite clearly...

"the DO-variable of the DO-loop can neither be redefined nor become
undefined during execution of the range of the DO-loop. It is your
responsibility to ensure that such redefinitions don't occur."

Ignoring this, I tried to alter the DO-variable as you suggested, but the
compiler didn't like that one bit! ...

DO 1501 II = 1 , 12
II = 13
1501 CONTINUE
*ERROR 1902 at line 550 Assignment result 'II' is an active DO variable

So, it seems the responsibility wasn't mine at all! :) (as mentioned in
the manual).

Silly bloody thing... but that's FORTRAN for you! When I started work here
8 years ago, I already thought FORTRAN was dead... and I'm STILL coding in
it!!!

I can only hope AMOS lasts as long!

	Message #1350 of 8200 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

YAMOG

Wed Oct 7, 1998 10:57 am
"floquet" <floquet@hp-sc.univ-lille2.fr>


(Yet Another Message About Goto) 8)

Hello,
Here are some personal opinions:

Concerning the trick consisting of changing the value of the iterator in
the loop is... a trick !
You'd better use this:

I=MINVALUE
COND=False
While (Not COND) and (I <= MAXVALUE)
'(code setting somewhere COND to True)
Add I, MYSTEPVALUE
Wend

I've been a professional programmer for more than 10 years. Understand
"I'm paid for this" and not "I am a genius" 8))
I've been programming for more than 15 years.
Computing is a science. So there are rules to be respected. When I was
studying comp-science, no teacher told us about GOTO.
I don't intend to teach you how to do, but there are 4 main structures
used in programming, in EVERY language :
- The sequence : Some instructions one after the other
- The condition : If/Then/Else/Endif
- The unconditional loop : For/Next
- The onditional loop : While/Wend or Repeat/Until.
A code respecting these structures can be easyly ported into another
language (Amos->C, QBASIC->Amos, Amos->DbaseIII, etc...)
There is no place for Goto in these structures, except for low-level
languages, where you need to convert:
REPEAT LABEL1:
blabla >>Into>> blabla
UNTIL CONDITION IF not CONDITION GOTO LABEL1

Concerning EXITs, POP PROCs and other ways to quit a loop, a program (or
procedure, subroutine,etc) must have a beginning, a body and an end.
Using Exits or Pop procs don't allow the end of a procedure where you
could do some interesting things.

You can find the equivalent in other professions:
For example, you can put at home a wallpaper upon another, but pros
don't, they remove the old one before. The result is the same : You get
a blue room.

You are FREE to use gotos, I don't want to disgust you (all) from using
Amiga & Amos. Hobbyists are not bad programmers because they use GOTOs.
Pros just prefer to use the good old rules. Experience shows that a prog
without GOTOs is easier to debug or enhance. It works better, too,
because you _have_to_ analyse your needs before coding.

One last thing : Even some Pros use Gotos !

I apologise for being long, but I had to say that.
--

 /____   ____/\       /   /
 \___/  __/\_\/ *____/   / AMIGA
    /__/\_\/     \  /   / POWER
    \__\/         \/___/INSIDE

> For REP3=1 To 1000
> If NEEDTOEXIT
> REP3=1001 : REP2=101 : REP1=11
> End If
> Next REP3
> Next REP2
> Next REP1
>
> That's the method I use in AMOS, BLITZ, C, etc. Of course, you can
> Pop out of AMOS and BLITZ's loop I believe, but I have always found
> it's easier to find a good solution then stick to it... that's part of
> the benefit of choosing the "right" solution... it is 100% portable
> between languages.
>
>
>> That logic has always confused me, and for a long time I wasnt sure
>> will Repeat Until condition be looped if condition is true or false.
>> Bwyatt in POP had a solution to this:
>> Do While... Loop
>> Do...Loop While
>> Do Until... Loop
>> Do... Loop Until
>> You could even make combinations like:
>> Do While... Loop Until
>> We should convince him to continue work ;)
>
> Haha... yes, Ben is a clever guy. Hmm... that idea about the
> combination looks a bit strange, now doesn't it? We have a Do While
> loop condition at the top combined with a Repeat Until condition at
> the bottom... very unique. Ben what were you thinking there? Was
> this simply to illustrate that the programmer has complete flexibility??
>
> Okay, this has been interesting... talking about programming style is
> always a good thing, but we better stop and get back to pure AMOS,
> and I think that's where this thread began... :-)
>

hey! can we stop this now i'm sure GOTO is completley fed up! And just wants
to be loved!

	Message #1363 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: A Study In Loop Exiting... GENERAL

Wed Oct 7, 1998 5:19 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> Here are some personal opinions:
> Concerning the trick consisting of changing the value of the iterator in
> the loop is... a trick !
> You'd better use this:
> I=MINVALUE
> COND=False
> While (Not COND) and (I <= MAXVALUE)
> '(code setting somewhere COND to True)
> Add I, MYSTEPVALUE
> Wend

Exactly... I agree. I generally use a While structure... they are made
to allow premature exiting, so to speak. In AMOS, of course you can
use Repeat... Until in the same manner.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #1364 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: GOTOs

Wed Oct 7, 1998 5:24 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> If NEEDTOEXIT
> REP3=1001 : REP2=101 : REP1=11
> Why not use Exit(3) instead ?
> End If

Because, I'm pretty sure that Pascal doesn't support that... haha.

The original poster said he was unable to find a way to exit from nested
loops in Pascal... I have found that the above works fine BASIC, C and
C++, and obviously Assembler.

However, it is worth mentioning that you should rely on one of the While
or even Repeat loop structures if you are planning on prematurely
exiting the loops, they were designed to handle that.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

Uhm, If you can't use libs then I advise you not to touch extension
coding for the time been 8o)
You'll need a much bigger and complex understanding of the amigas chips,
the CPU you code for( TGE is coded for 030...) and you'll need librarys
the whole time, espically exec. All the librarys you'll need will be
in the ROMS, so no files will be needed.

PS: Although Ive said TGE is coded for 030, it works on 000 but
030 for best performance on the tmapping and such(complex gfx).

about the poor old Goto command! There it is just minding its own business,
and here you all go moaning about it! Oh well... never mind! I guess no one
here i listening to me!

>Hello,
>Here are some personal opinions:
>
>Concerning the trick consisting of changing the value of the iterator in
>the loop is... a trick !
>You'd better use this:
>
>I=MINVALUE
>COND=False
>While (Not COND) and (I <= MAXVALUE)
> '(code setting somewhere COND to True)
> Add I, MYSTEPVALUE
>Wend
>
>I've been a professional programmer for more than 10 years. Understand
>"I'm paid for this" and not "I am a genius" 8))
>I've been programming for more than 15 years.
>Computing is a science. So there are rules to be respected. When I was
>studying comp-science, no teacher told us about GOTO.
>I don't intend to teach you how to do, but there are 4 main structures
>used in programming, in EVERY language :
>- The sequence : Some instructions one after the other
>- The condition : If/Then/Else/Endif
>- The unconditional loop : For/Next
>- The onditional loop : While/Wend or Repeat/Until.
>A code respecting these structures can be easyly ported into another
>language (Amos->C, QBASIC->Amos, Amos->DbaseIII, etc...)
>There is no place for Goto in these structures, except for low-level
>languages, where you need to convert:
>REPEAT LABEL1:
> blabla >>Into>> blabla
>UNTIL CONDITION IF not CONDITION GOTO LABEL1
>

Yep! I agree!

>Concerning EXITs, POP PROCs and other ways to quit a loop, a program (or
>procedure, subroutine,etc) must have a beginning, a body and an end.
>Using Exits or Pop procs don't allow the end of a procedure where you
>could do some interesting things.
>
>You can find the equivalent in other professions:
>For example, you can put at home a wallpaper upon another, but pros
>don't, they remove the old one before. The result is the same : You get
>a blue room.

Cool! Analogy!

>
>You are FREE to use gotos, I don't want to disgust you (all) from using
>Amiga & Amos. Hobbyists are not bad programmers because they use GOTOs.
>Pros just prefer to use the good old rules. Experience shows that a prog
>without GOTOs is easier to debug or enhance. It works better, too,
>because you _have_to_ analyse your needs before coding.


Yep!

>One last thing : Even some Pros use Gotos !


I know! People Have different Program Styles!

On 06-Okt-98, Garfield Benjamin wrote:

GB>> Well, I'm not a really really good programmer speaking both about
GB>> my programs and amount of theory I know (very little). But I don't
GB>> want to be dogmatic about anything, and if I couldn't think of a good
GB>> example for Goto, I would probably reply that there might be some
GB>> cases where Goto is usable, but I don't know them.

GB> Well, in a previous post I said that I don't think Goto is completely
GB> useless, but rather it is completely unnecessary due to advances in
GB> programming languages. It's another question whether being
GB> unnecessary equals useless. It's all a matter of style really... of
GB> course you could use Goto in loads of places and anyone is obviously
GB> free to do so, but some of us are simply saying there are better ways
GB> to handle this... for every place someone might use a Goto, we could
GB> provide a "non-Goto" (copyright 1998 Garfield Benjamin) solution.

Well, you could always use While instead of For, but that wouldn't make
nice programs... I just said that there are some very rare occasions when
Goto is the best solution, that's all.

GB>> Have you seen all programs in the world, so that you can tell that
GB>> there is not a single usable Goto in them?

GB> As a matter of fact I have... haha. Of course I have not seen every
GB> program in the world, but then I do not need to. I have seen and

I knew it ;)

GB> It's really a matter of preference and programming is a very personal
GB> thing... we each have our own style to a degree and no one can say
GB> what is right or wrong for someone else, we only know what is
GB> right for ourselves. However, there are certain aspects of
GB> programming which are universally true and structured programming
GB> or object oriented programming introduced new methods which are
GB> "better" in many ways.

I agree with you completely.

GB> Why not simply set your loop variables to equal the EndLoop states?
GB> Example in AMOS code ( to help us stay focused )

GB> For REP1=1 To 10
GB> For REP2=1 To 100
GB> For REP3=1 To 1000
GB> If NEEDTOEXIT
GB> REP3=1001 : REP2=101 : REP1=11
GB> End If
GB> Next REP3
GB> Next REP2
GB> Next REP1

GB> That's the method I use in AMOS, BLITZ, C, etc. Of course, you can

It's OK, except that it doesn't skip any code you might have between loops,
it isn't obvious for what it does, and it changes REP values which are
sometimes needed.

GB> Pop out of AMOS and BLITZ's loop I believe, but I have always found
GB> it's easier to find a good solution then stick to it... that's part
of
GB> the benefit of choosing the "right" solution... it is 100% portable
GB> between languages.

Even in Fortran? ;)

GB>> That logic has always confused me, and for a long time I wasnt sure
GB>> will Repeat Until condition be looped if condition is true or false.
GB>> Bwyatt in POP had a solution to this:
GB>> Do While... Loop
GB>> Do...Loop While
GB>> Do Until... Loop
GB>> Do... Loop Until
GB>> You could even make combinations like:
GB>> Do While... Loop Until
GB>> We should convince him to continue work ;)

GB> Haha... yes, Ben is a clever guy. Hmm... that idea about the
GB> combination looks a bit strange, now doesn't it? We have a Do While

I think that it would be rarely be used, but if a need arises, it could be
useful.

GB> loop condition at the top combined with a Repeat Until condition at
GB> the bottom... very unique. Ben what were you thinking there? Was

I don't know about any other language which has it. Of course, any
combination of While and Until is possible, maybe even with Do For loops
(which is a nice way to exit them ;)

GB> this simply to illustrate that the programmer has complete
flexibility??

Another similar construction is If a<b<c<d ;)

GB> Okay, this has been interesting... talking about programming style is
GB> always a good thing, but we better stop and get back to pure AMOS,
GB> and I think that's where this thread began... :-)

Well, everything we say could and will be used (against us ;) in Amos. I

Re: hiya

Thu Oct 8, 1998 8:55 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 06-Okt-98, John Glanville wrote:

JG>>> heres a list of someof the things that I can do with calls!

JG>>> Point(X,Y))
JG>>> Draw, Bar, Box, and circle on Pub screens.
JG>>> Clear Screen!
JG>>> WriteText - I'm still tryin to figure the Flags for this one!

graphics.library/Text

NAME
Text -- Write text characters (no formatting).

SYNOPSIS
Text(rp, string, length)
A1 A0 D0-0:16

void Text(struct RastPort *, STRPTR, WORD);

FUNCTION
This graphics function writes printable text characters to the
specified RastPort at the current position. No control meaning
is applied to any of the characters, thus only text on the
current line is output.

The current position in the RastPort is updated to the next
character position.
If the characters displayed run past the RastPort boundary,
the current position is truncated to the boundary, and
thus does not equal the old position plus the text length.

INPUTS
rp - a pointer to the RastPort which describes where the
text is to be output
string - the address of string to output
length - the number of characters in the string.
If zero, there are no characters to be output.

JG>>> Return the WB + Screen + Window rastport
JG>>> Make your own Guru Alert!
JG>>> Execute a Program!
JG>>
JG>> Where did you find how to do that stuff ? Can you tell us how to do
the
JG>> same, please ?
JG>> (I'm prying you on my knees 8)

	Message #1385 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: On the topic of GOTOs

Fri Oct 9, 1998 2:39 am
"Chris Coulson" <chris@bay13.demon.co.uk>


> Stacey Abshire commented:
>
> Do you guys have nothing better to do? When it all comes right down to
> it, EVERY program that has any sort of loop structure has a GOTO in it.

Not true, which is precisely why this discussion is so valuable...
Every GOTO is a jump, but not every jump is a GOTO.

> Whether it is a WHILE loop with the WEND GOTO, or whether it is a FOR loop
> with the NEXT GOTO, etc, etc, etc...

Aaarghhhhhhhh!!! Loop constructs *don`t* GOTO, they JUMP. A GOTO is
a programmer-defined jump to any point in the program, a loop
construct jump can *only* jump back to the start of the construct.
And since GOTO gives us that much power, we can use it to do some
highly stupid things...

Consider this perfectly legal piece of AMOS code:

A
1 Stop

Procedure A
B
2 Goto 1
End Proc

Procedure B
Goto 2
End Proc


This is, quite simply, an appalingly bad piece of code. And only
GOTO makes it possible... Now, whilst no-one in their right mind
would ever write a piece of code that was so obviously wrong, if
you`re developing a long program with GOTOs, then it`s possible that
you might inadvertantly create something with the same structure. If
you don`t use GOTO, it`s impossible to make this mistake.

> This is boring, and most uninformative.

It`ll be uninformative once everyone is aware of the problems that
GOTO introduces, not before...

Fact is, with the exception of certain languages that have no
alternative, the use of GOTO (or the equivalent command) is shunned
by any serious programmer, with good reason. We`re not making this
up, GOTO really is a dangerous command when misused, and it`s all too
easy to accidentally misuse it.


Chris

--
                          At Home With the Chris
         Amigas, Babylon 5, Flight Sims, RIAT'97-98 and Melanie C
                       http://www.tornado.pair.com/

Hello Stephen

On 08-Ott-98, Stephen Thornber wrote: [amos-list] un-iconify

> From: Stephen Thornber <SThornber@steve1.demon.co.uk>
>
>
>
> Hi all
>
> I still can't read the damn close gadget when my prog is
> iconified.. I've treid reading the docs, but no help there.

Read the doc carefully :))) Expecially the Gui Wait command.


> my code is:-
>
> Gui Iconify(1)
> Do
> GW=Gui Wait
> If GW=-1
> Gui Uniconify(1)
> EndIf
> Loop
>
> But it doesn't work :(

When a GUI is iconified, if you press the close gadget Gui Wait returns -6
(..uniconify message) and not -1.

so your code is:

Gui Iconify(1)
Do
GW=Gui Wait
If GW=-6
Gui Uniconify(1)
EndIf
Loop

> It iconify's great, but won't uniconify.. doh!

Nope :) Enoy.... the GUI Extension V2 will offer TRUE iconify using AppIcons
and a Iconify gadget in the window title bar like MUI.

>graphics.library/Text
>
> NAME
> Text -- Write text characters (no formatting).
>
> SYNOPSIS
> Text(rp, string, length)
> A1 A0 D0-0:16
>
> void Text(struct RastPort *, STRPTR, WORD);
>
> FUNCTION
> This graphics function writes printable text characters to the
> specified RastPort at the current position. No control meaning
> is applied to any of the characters, thus only text on the
> current line is output.
>
> The current position in the RastPort is updated to the next
> character position.
> If the characters displayed run past the RastPort boundary,
> the current position is truncated to the boundary, and
> thus does not equal the old position plus the text length.
>
> INPUTS
> rp - a pointer to the RastPort which describes where the
> text is to be output
> string - the address of string to output
> length - the number of characters in the string.
> If zero, there are no characters to be output.
>

to do it.... but good description! Is that yours or is it from somewhere

	Message #1400 of 8205

Re: On the topic of GOTOs

Fri Oct 9, 1998 10:39 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


-----Original Message-----
From: Chris Coulson <chris@bay13.demon.co.uk>
To: Amos List <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 09 October 1998 02:34
Subject: [amos-list] Re: On the topic of GOTOs


>From: "Chris Coulson" <chris@bay13.demon.co.uk>
>
>> Stacey Abshire commented:
>>

La La La!!!! Hmmmm! We're not still talking about this?

>> Do you guys have nothing better to do? When it all comes right down to
>> it, EVERY program that has any sort of loop structure has a GOTO in it.
>
>Not true, which is precisely why this discussion is so valuable...
>Every GOTO is a jump, but not every jump is a GOTO.
>
>> Whether it is a WHILE loop with the WEND GOTO, or whether it is a FOR
loop
>> with the NEXT GOTO, etc, etc, etc...
>
>Aaarghhhhhhhh!!! Loop constructs *don`t* GOTO, they JUMP. A GOTO is
>a programmer-defined jump to any point in the program, a loop
>construct jump can *only* jump back to the start of the construct.
>And since GOTO gives us that much power, we can use it to do some
>highly stupid things...
>
>Consider this perfectly legal piece of AMOS code:
>
>A
>1 Stop
>
>Procedure A
>B
>2 Goto 1
>End Proc
>
>Procedure B
>Goto 2
>End Proc
>
>
>This is, quite simply, an appalingly bad piece of code. And only
>GOTO makes it possible... Now, whilst no-one in their right mind
>would ever write a piece of code that was so obviously wrong, if
>you`re developing a long program with GOTOs, then it`s possible that
>you might inadvertantly create something with the same structure. If
>you don`t use GOTO, it`s impossible to make this mistake.
>
>> This is boring, and most uninformative.
>
>It`ll be uninformative once everyone is aware of the problems that
>GOTO introduces, not before...
>
>Fact is, with the exception of certain languages that have no
>alternative, the use of GOTO (or the equivalent command) is shunned
>by any serious programmer, with good reason. We`re not making this
>up, GOTO really is a dangerous command when misused, and it`s all too
>easy to accidentally misuse it.
>
>
>Chris
>
>--
> At Home With the Chris
> Amigas, Babylon 5, Flight Sims, RIAT'97-98 and Melanie C
> http://www.tornado.pair.com/
>

	Message #1417 of 8205

Re: Gotos everywhere...

Sun Oct 11, 1998 10:52 pm
"Chris Coulson" <chris@bay13.demon.co.uk>


> >Not true, which is precisely why this discussion is so valuable... Every
> >GOTO is a jump, but not every jump is a GOTO.
>
> I don't guess you have used assembly have you?

Wrong. And it`s partly because I have used asm that I know what a
misused "goto" can do to a program. When you have to take care of
the stack yourself, you get pretty paranoid about making sure your
program flow between subroutines is absolutely correct. And if you
could have seen some of the convoluted student code I`ve had to try
sorting out in asm practical sessions, you`d know why I`m so against
the use of arbitrary leaps from A to B, such as GOTO permits.

Even in asm, it`s quite easy to think in terms of WHILE WEND or
whatever, and write your loops accordingly. That you`re using a jmp
or a bgt or a dbne or whatever is beside the point - you as the
programmer *know* what that jump represents. It`s when you start
using branch/jump commands without them mapping onto some higher
construct that the problems start - in other words, when you start
using them as if they were GOTO`s...
I can`t recall the last time I ever used a branch in asm without it
being part of such a higher construct, just as I can`t recall the
last time I ever used GOTO in AMOS (examples of GOTO misuse aside :-)

The point I was trying to make with that GOTO/jump comment earlier is
that you as the programmer don`t use GOTO to return to the start of a
loop in AMOS, you use WEND, UNTIL, NEXT etc. They`re all jumps, but
they`re not all GOTO`s. You *only* use GOTO if you want to introduce
a jump that has no other purpose in life other than to jump
unconditionally from A to B - it isn`t part of a loop, it isn`t part
of a subroutine call, it`s just a jump. And in all the languages I`m
familiar with, there is NO good software-related excuse for doing
this. Hardware limitations may be an excuse, but not in AMOS`s case.

> it, your AMOS code, C code, Pascal, or whatever, will use in essence a
> GOTO. A JMP command is a GOTO.

Only if you choose to use it like that, and it`s also (when combined
with other mnemonics) a WEND, UNTIL, NEXT etc. OTOH, there`s no need
to combine GOTO with other commands in AMOS to achieve a WEND or
whatever, because the language already provides those commands
directly. So the only thing that GOTO is good for is unstructured
leaping around, which is bad.

JMP *can* do the same, but it doesn`t *have* to. And unless they`ve
got a superb reason for doing so (embedded controller programming
with limited memory springs to mind here), any semi-competent asm
programmer isn`t going to use JMP as a GOTO, because poor programming
style is poor programming style, no matter what language you`re
using.


> I am condoning GOTO at all.

I really hope you left out the "not" in that comment.

> I just think that this is a useless discussion.

I wish it was, but there still seems to be a little bit too much
confusion over exactly what GOTO entails for the thread to die down.


Chris

The DevPac editor is rubbish, your best off to use CED or GoldED,

genam <srcfile> nocase
it wont be case sensitive.

	Message #1427 of 8205

OM functioning

Thu Oct 15, 1998 4:55 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


Hi again,

I'd just like to that Declan for passing on the OM coverdisk - it seems to
work just fine on the old A3000, so life will be a bit easier for me now
(no more passing disks between my A500 and A3000 !!)

In my playing around with Amos3D, I've already noticed some speed problems
and am having to compromise a little on detail to gain that little extra
oomph. But I'm quite pleased with what I DO have thus far. (If anyone's
interested: its gunna be a little 3D-type shoot'em'up based on the old
"War Of The Worlds" film from the '50's (plus some help from Jeff Wayne's
musical rendition) - I just love that HeatRay!

The OM (Object Modeller) is remarkably good, considering - I'd forgotten
just how easy it is to pick up the basics of it's use and produce quite
GOOD results! Naturally it isn't perfect, and some things are very
difficult to achieve (just FORGET about curved surfaces!) and it has
crashed my A500 numerous times (but I'm pretty sure that's related to an
old screen blanker (Blankette?) that I still use).

Anyway, that's it for now... I just wanted to post something totally
unrelated to GOTO's and unnecessary file attachments!

Wish me luck!

Phil 8-)

	Message #1432 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: AMOS Pro & MUI

Thu Oct 15, 1998 3:29 pm
Michel Donat <Michel.Donat@wanadoo.fr>


Hello Declan

Le 15-Oct-98, Declan Gorman a écrit:

> Has anyone worked successfully with MUI interfaces in AMOS Pro? Is it
> possible?

Yes i'm make an API procedures for AmosPro and MUI
I use the Easylife and the osdevkit extensions .


> My next project requires more of a GUI than the standard workbench GUI has
> to offer and I am looking into using an MUI interface.

So i'm make again the ClassAct APi same MUI ;-)

The probleme for MUI is the not possibility to make 'Hook' for some MUI
custom class or gadgets :-(


ClassAct is very easy to use.


------------------------------------------------------------
Here is an example to use the MUI procedures :
------------------------------------------------------------

_OPEN_MUI_LIB

_INIT_APPLICATION : If Param : APP_TAG=Param

_MUI_WINDOW[_to Str("Essai MUI"),_val.l("MAIN")] : If Param : WND_TAG=Param

'
' Definition Menu
'
_MENUSTRIP : If Param : MENU_TAG=Param

_MENU[_to Str("Project")] : If Param : MENU=Param

_MENU_ITEM[MENU,2,_to Str("A Propos"),_to Str("?"),1]
_MENU_BAR[MENU]
_MENU_ITEM[MENU,3,_to Str("Load"),_to Str("L"),1]
_MENU_BAR[MENU]
_MENU_CHECK[MENU,4,_to Str("Checkit"),_to Str("C"),1]

_END_MENU[MENU_TAG,MENU,1] : End If

_END_MENUSTRIP[WND_TAG,MENU_TAG] : End If
'
' Definition Layout Principal
'
_MUI_VGROUPE[0] : If Param : MAIN=Param

_MUIB_TEXTBUTTON[MAIN,-1,_to Str("MUI Demo © 1998 Donat Michel"),1]

_MUI_HGROUPE[0] : If Param : GRP=Param

'
' Here i use the Toolbar.mcc MUI Custom Class
'
_MAIN_TOOLBAR : BANK1=Param
NORMAL$="PROGDIR:MainBar.ILBM"
SELECT$="PROGDIR:MainBar_S.ILBM"
GHOSTED$="PROGDIR:MainBar_G.ILBM"

_MUIB_TOOLBAR[GRP,-1,BANK1,NORMAL$,SELECT$,GHOSTED$]
_MUIB_RECTANGLE[GRP]
_MUI_ADD_GROUPE[MAIN,GRP] : End If

_MUIB_NLISTVIEW[MAIN,0]

TITLE=_vec Alloc(12,$10001)
Loke TITLE,_to Str("Consultation")
Loke TITLE+4,_to Str("Edition")

_MUI_REGISTER[TITLE,1] : If Param : PAGE_TAG=Param

_MUI_VGROUPE[0] : If Param : GRP=Param

_MUIB_LABEL_TEXTBUTTON[GRP,10,_to Str("Titre"),_to
Str("Poireaux"),0]
_MUIB_TEXTEDITOR[GRP,-1]

_MUI_ADD_GROUPE[PAGE_TAG,GRP] : End If


_MUI_VGROUPE[0] : If Param : GRP=Param

_MUIB_LABEL_STRING[GRP,10,_to Str("_Titre"),_to
Str("Poireaux"),20]

_EDIT_TOOLBAR : BANK2=Param
NORMAL$="PROGDIR:Toolstrip.ILBM"
SELECT$="PROGDIR:toolstrip_S.ILBM"
GHOSTED$="PROGDIR:Toolstrip_G.ILBM"

_MUI_HGROUPE[0] : If Param : GRP1=Param
_MUIB_TOOLBAR[GRP1,-1,BANK2,NORMAL$,SELECT$,GHOSTED$]
_MUIB_RECTANGLE[GRP1]
_MUI_ADD_GROUPE[GRP,GRP1] : End If

_MUIB_LABEL_CYCLE[GRP,21,_to Str("_Couleur"),_gt Make
Array(Array(MOI$(0)))]

_MUIB_TEXTEDITOR[GRP,-1]

_MUI_ADD_GROUPE[PAGE_TAG,GRP] : End If

_MUI_END_REGISTER[MAIN,PAGE_TAG] : End If



_MUI_HGROUPE[0] : If Param : GRP=Param

_MUIB_BUTTON[GRP,22,_to Str("_Ajoute")]
_MUIB_BUTTON[GRP,23,_to Str("Efface")]
_MUIB_BUTTON[GRP,23,_to Str("Imprime")]

_MUI_ADD_GROUPE[MAIN,GRP] : End If

_MUI_END_GROUPE[MAIN,20] : ROOT_OBJ=Param : End If

_MUI_WINDOW_ROOT_OBJECT[WND_TAG,ROOT_OBJ]
_MUI_END_WINDOW[APP_TAG,WND_TAG,ROOT_OBJ] : WIN=Param
End If

_END_APPLICATION[APP_TAG] : APP_OBJ=Param : End If
If Param=0
_print "Failed to create apllication !"
Goto FIN
End If


------------------------------------------------------------
Here is an example to use the ClassAct procedures :
------------------------------------------------------------

_VGROUP[-1,0,0,0] : MAIN_TAG=Param

_HGROUP[-1,0,-1,-1] : G_TAG=Param

_CLASSACT_SIMPLE_LISTBROWSER[G_TAG,100,LB_LIST,0]
_CHILD_MINWIDTH[G_TAG,100]
_CHILD_WEIGHTEDWIDTH[G_TAG,0]

_HGROUP[-1,0,0,0] : G1_TAG=Param

_STARTPAGE : PAGE_TAG=Param

_ADD_VPAGE[8,0,0,0] : P_TAG=Param

_CLASSACT_IMAGE[P_TAG,"amos_sources:gest'fiches/gestfiches_logo.iff",16]
_END_PAGE[PAGE_TAG,P_TAG]

_ADD_VPAGE[2,0,-1,-1] : P_TAG=Param
_CLASSACT_BEVEL[P_TAG,3,102,_to Str("Page 1"),3,2]
_CHILD_MINHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CHILD_MAXHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CHILD_MINWIDTH[P_TAG,150]
_CLASSACT_TEXTEDITOR[P_TAG,2,0] : _EDITOR=Param
_END_PAGE[PAGE_TAG,P_TAG]

_ADD_VPAGE[2,0,-1,-1] : P_TAG=Param
_CLASSACT_BEVEL[P_TAG,3,102,_to Str("Page 2"),3,2]
_CHILD_MINHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CHILD_MAXHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CLASSACT_CHOOSER[P_TAG,5,_CHOOSERLIST_VALIDE,0]
_CHILD_LABEL[P_TAG,_to Str("_Choix")]
_CLASSACT_LISTBROWSER[P_TAG,1,0,0,0]
_CHILD_MINWIDTH[P_TAG,150]
_CLASSACT_STRING[P_TAG,2,_to Str("essai"),12,4]
_END_PAGE[PAGE_TAG,P_TAG]

_ADD_VPAGE[2,0,-1,-1] : P_TAG=Param
_CLASSACT_BEVEL[P_TAG,3,102,_to Str("Page 3"),3,2]
_CHILD_MINHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CHILD_MAXHEIGHT[P_TAG,25]
_CLASSACT_SIMPLE_LISTBROWSER[P_TAG,1,LB_LIST,0]
_END_PAGE[PAGE_TAG,P_TAG]

_END_STARTPAGE[G1_TAG,PAGE_TAG] : PAGE_GADGET=Param

_ADD_END_GROUP[G_TAG,G1_TAG] : LAYOUT_PAGE_GADGET=Param

_ADD_END_GROUP[MAIN_TAG,G_TAG]

_HGROUP[4,0,-1,-1] : G_TAG=Param
_CLASSACT_BUTTON[G_TAG,1,LABEL1]
_CLASSACT_BUTTON[G_TAG,2,LABEL2]
_CLASSACT_BUTTON[G_TAG,3,LABEL3]
_ADD_END_GROUP[MAIN_TAG,G_TAG] : GROUP1=Param

_CHILD_WEIGHTEDHEIGHT[MAIN_TAG,0]

_END_GROUP[MAIN_TAG] : OBJ=Param

Regards
--
A+

Michel.

E-Mail: Michel.Donat@wanadoo.fr

	Message #1435 of 8205

Re: Welcome to amos-list@onelist.com

Thu Oct 15, 1998 4:35 pm
Ken <cbminfo@digital.net>


>You are now subscribed to the list. In order to send a message to everyone
on
>the list, mail the message to:

I was subscribed ages ago. But never folloewd thru with getting blitz or amos.

At that time when I was looking for an amiga basic compiler I heard about
ACE. And picked it up from aminet, did a little experimentation with it.
contacted David Benn re:ACE (He's the author). Though he has discontinued
development by him on ACE, he's released the full source code. I created an
ACE mailing list here at onelist to hopefully get people interested in
customizing and upgrading ACE to what WE want in a basic compiler. Did I
mention it's FREE ?

ACE was and is fully functional as is. Those of us on the list now are hoping
to make ACE even better.

Come on over, you could learn something about C and basic programming as we
work out the upgrades to ACE..

On Break Broke?

Fri Oct 16, 1998 1:05 am
Bob Jordan <bjordan@soest.hawaii.edu>


What am I doing wrong? I can't seem to get any of the ON BREAKs to work.
I've tried procedures, gosubs, and goto and none seem to work. The
Procedure complains of a syntax error, and the gosub and goto forms are
ignored as if the ON BREAK statement is not being recognized. Also the
help example has comments about this statement, but doesn't actually
implement them in the program. I entered the commented program and got
same results. Any clues would be appreciated. Following is what I tried:

On Break Proc BROKEN1
Do
Print "unbroken"
Wait 10
Loop

Procedure BROKEN1
Print "broke out of loop"
End Proc
'-----

On BREAK Gosub BROKEN2
Do
Print "unbroken"
Wait 10
Loop

BROKEN2:
Print "broke out of loop"
Return
'-----

On BREAK Goto BROKEN3
Do
Print "unbroken"
Wait 10
Loop

BROKEN3 :
Print "broke out of loop"
End
'-----

Re: On Break Broke?

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as Bob,
> What am I doing wrong? I can't seem to get any of the ON BREAKs to work.
> I've tried procedures, gosubs, and goto and none seem to work. The
> Procedure complains of a syntax error, and the gosub and goto forms are
> ignored as if the ON BREAK statement is not being recognized. Also the
> help example has comments about this statement, but doesn't actually
> implement them in the program. I entered the commented program and got
> same results. Any clues would be appreciated. Following is what I tried:
> On Break Proc BROKEN1

nnnng.

I hate on break. Oh well. You could do this:

break off
while loop=1
do whatever.
gosub breakcheck
wend
end

breakcheck:
q$=inkey$
if q$=chr$(3)
loop=0
' error 42 rem or something.
end if
return

Or something like that if you wanted to check for ctrl-c. I don't personally
mess with break checks much.

is done by request from Rune, as soon as we solve some minor technical
problems the two sites will be merged into one, but for now the listings
are made as 'stand-alone' pages..

on the site in the future. Please send me any ideas you have to improve
existing sections, or to make new ones, to me.

and there's one/some you think noone should live without then let me know.

you who hated the old version....

through my 'main page'...

> checking for a break which eats more execution time.

Hmmm, ok, see ammendment....

Actually, afaik, amos treats break checks as busy. Ghizzo ?

> Is there a way to make ON BREAK work or is it truly broke?

Yes, but it's a dodgy command, and it's very tricky inside procedures, and
makes the whole thing a mess. Actually most of the interupt stuff in amos
is a bit dodgy.


> > break off
> > while loop=1
> > do whatever.
> > gosub breakcheck
> > wend
> > end

> > breakcheck:
> > q$=inkey$
wait vbl
> > if q$=chr$(3)
> > loop=0
> > ' error 42 rem or something.
> > end if
> > return

you just tell it the screen to use in init() instead of doing it for ever c2p.

Mon Oct 19, 1998 4:58 am

search an array, preferably with pattern matching options. The AMOSPro 'Match'
command only works at all after a sort (I'm searching about 7,000 items, so

the Jd Extension, but it's poorly documented, and I couldn't get it to work. I

since; before I start hassling him, has anyone else had this problem?)

	Message #1452 of 8205

Re: Searching an array

Mon Oct 19, 1998 7:07 am
<Magnus.Sjoberg@asdo.se>


> Rod Whiteley <rwhiteley@magnet.com.au> wrote:
>
>Dear AMOSer's
>Any ideas?
>I'm altering a search utility, and would to know if there's a
command to
>search an array, preferably with pattern matching options. The
AMOSPro 'Match'
>command only works at all after a sort (I'm searching about 7,000
items, so
>this takes ages) and doesn't work very accurately. I note there's a
command in
>the Jd Extension, but it's poorly documented, and I couldn't get it
to work. I
>couldn't find an AMCAF command (which surprised me.)

Try this:
Result=Jd Compare(STEACH_CRITERIA,STRING_TO_CHECK)
Wildcards (* and ?) can be used.
Result=True if match found.

Example:
If Jd Compare("AMO*","AMOS Pro")
Print "Match found !"
End If

It should be something like that.
I don't got the "manual" in front of me though.

Regards
Magnus

	Message #1456 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: CD32 and Hires

Mon Oct 19, 1998 9:11 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

>> Also I've asked about this before. Is there any support for CD32
>> joysticks thru AMOS. If so, could someone send me a code fragment.

> TGE has cd32 pad support, but for it you will have to wait
> until Nov15th.


That is incorrect. you CAN use CD32 pads with out /any/ extensions:


All you need is to call the Lowlevel library.


Heres some example code:


--------------------------------------------------------
'
' CD32 Joypad
'
' (c) K.Hill, Jan 1996
'
'
'structures begin
'
'Const JPF_BUTTON_FORWARD=$80000
'Const JPF_LEFT = 2
'Const JPF_JOY_UP = 8
'Const JPF_BUTTON_REVERSE = $40000
'Const JPF_DOWN = 4
'Const JPF_JOY_RIGHT = 1
'Const JPF_JOY_LEFT = 2
'Const JPF_BUTTON_GREEN = $100000
'Const JPF_BUTTON_YELLOW = $200000
'Const JPF_JOY_DOWN = 4
'Const JPF_BUTTON_BLUE = $800000
'Const JPF_UP = 8
'Const JPF_BUTTON_PLAY = $20000
'Const JPF_BTN1 = $800000
'Const JPF_BTN2 = $400000
'Const JPF_BTN3 = $200000
'Const JPF_BTN4 = $100000
'Const JPF_BTN5 = $80000
'Const JPF_RIGHT = 1
'Const JPF_BTN6 = $40000
'Const JPF_BTN7 = $20000
'Const JPF_BUTTON_RED = $400000
'
'Structures Constants

Global __JPF_BUTTON_FORWARD,__JPF_LEFT,__JPF_JOY_UP
__JPF_BUTTON_FORWARD=524288 : __JPF_LEFT=2 : __JPF_JOY_UP=8
Global __JPF_BUTTON_REVERSE,__JPF_DOWN,__JPF_JOY_RIGHT
__JPF_BUTTON_REVERSE=262144 : __JPF_DOWN=4 : __JPF_JOY_RIGHT=1
Global __JPF_JOY_LEFT,__JPF_BUTTON_GREEN,__JPF_BUTTON_YELLOW
__JPF_JOY_LEFT=2 : __JPF_BUTTON_GREEN=1048576 :
__JPF_BUTTON_YELLOW=2097152
Global __JPF_JOY_DOWN,__JPF_BUTTON_BLUE,__JPF_UP
__JPF_JOY_DOWN=4 : __JPF_BUTTON_BLUE=8388608 : __JPF_UP=8
Global __JPF_BUTTON_PLAY,__JPF_BTN1,__JPF_BTN2
__JPF_BUTTON_PLAY=131072 : __JPF_BTN1=8388608 : __JPF_BTN2=4194304
Global __JPF_BTN3,__JPF_BTN4,__JPF_BTN5,__JPF_RIGHT
__JPF_BTN3=2097152 : __JPF_BTN4=1048576 : __JPF_BTN5=524288 :
__JPF_RIGHT=1
Global __JPF_BTN6,__JPF_BTN7,__JPF_BUTTON_RED
__JPF_BTN6=262144 : __JPF_BTN7=131072 : __JPF_BUTTON_RED=4194304

'structures end

Lib Open 1,"lowlevel.library",40

Dreg(0)=1

'Dreg(0)=0
'
' This reads CD32 info. from the mouse port.
'


Do
Z=Lib Call(1,-30)
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_BLUE Then Print "Blue"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_RED Then Print "Red"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_GREEN Then Print "Green"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_YELLOW Then Print "Yellow"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_PLAY Then Print "Play"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_FORWARD Then Print "FF"
If Z and __JPF_BUTTON_REVERSE Then Print "Rew"
If Z and __JPF_JOY_DOWN Then Print "Down"
If Z and __JPF_JOY_UP Then Print "Up"
If Z and __JPF_JOY_LEFT Then Print "Left"
If Z and __JPF_JOY_RIGHT Then Print "Right"
Loop

--------------------------------------------------------



See ya.

	Message #1463 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Searching for a string

Tue Oct 20, 1998 5:47 pm
Bernie Noel <bnoel@club-internet.fr>


Hi listers,

Somebody asked about how to find a string in an array.
A quick way of finding a string in memory is the function Hunt:
Address=Hunt(start To finish,string$)

The problem with string arrays is that the strings are not stored in a
contiguous way (unlike numeric arrays). For instance A$(1) can be at one end
of the memory and A$(2) at the other end. (A slight exaggeration, but it's the
general idea).

So I'd recommend using a data bank instead of an array. The first chunk of the
bank could be used to store the offsets of the strings, and the rest of the
bank, the strings themselves.

If your purpose is making a Database, you might look into the "Random Access
Files" section too.

Best regards

Bernie

--
#Bernie Noel#, maker of *IMPERATOR*
http://www.amigaflame.co.uk/amii.htm
Email: <bnoel@club-internet.fr>
