	Message #1473 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Replies for all :)

Wed Oct 21, 1998 7:05 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hi!

i'm sorry for my fugitiveness, but in this period i've not many time for my
Amiga :(
Anyway now i'm here to reply to all the questions posted on the mailing-list
and other details.

Please find the time to read the full message, because it covers different
arguments :)

I've noticed the restart of 'Amos good, blitz bad"... mmmhhhh.. boring. No one
has really stress the difference... both Amos and Blitz are GOOD languages. The
REAL amos advantage over the others is only one:

most computer languages require that you think like a computer rather than a
human to work with it. AMOS works in human terms. All the functions and
commands are easy to learn due to the self-explaining names, and are easy to
use due to the AMOS philosophy 'i do everything for you'.
This is the reason of the Amos success.... several persons says' the Blitz is
faster'... yes is true, but it's no true!! You can't compare Blitz and Amos
because they works in a different way. Blitz works in a more 'low-level' way,
and is up to the user to code everything. The Blitz 'background' doesn't need
to check nothing.. if you're a good coder your programs will works fine, if you
sucks your programs will crash :) (.... for this reason the 70% of the blitz
programs crash soon or later)

Amos works in a high-level-human way. You can setup complex scenarios using few
commands... all the complex job is done in the Amos background. This is a
*good* and *bad* feature. It's good for the beginners, since they don't need
any programming/OS knowledge, is bad for the experienced users because they
can't
optmize the effect speed and the working method. Amos is 'slower' because it
needs to check tons of things in the background (several times uselessly),
and so it can't optimize the program execution.

If you're reading this, you prefer AMOS and its intuitive structure, so we
don't need to know that Blitz is bad :)

Another point.. i've received again some questions about the FD Extension...
probably i've not published enough my work :) First visit the AMOS Factory and
its download section, and get the FD Extension V2 archive. In the archive
you'll not find a Amos extension :) There is only the FD Builder. This cool
program allows you to real-time create AMOSPro extensions starting from
the standard .fd files of your preferred libraries. Just select some .fd
files,
and then click on the Build gadget... after few seconds a new extension with
ALL the functions described in the selected .fd files will be created and saved
in your APSytem directory. The advantage? Now you can use intuitive functions
calls
with their names instead of the offsets, and you don't need to know the
function registers.... example, graphics.library function Text:

Standard Amos method:

Areg(1)=RP : Areg(0)=varptr(T$) : Dreg(0)=Len(A$) : T=GfxCall(-xxx)


FD Extension:

T=Lvo Text(RP,ST,L)


much better no? You can use the function name, and pass the parameters without
remembering the right registers, everything will be setup correclty for you.
Now you can import as standard Amos commands all the libraries functions that
you
need like MUI, BsdSocket, etc, etc. without boring Areg(), Lib Open, Lib Call()
ecc. commands. The program will be faster too.. in the above example you use 1
command instead of 4 (..or more!) !!

What are you doing here? Download the FD extension kit!! it's freeware as
usual.


Several guys are looking for the AMOSPro Compiler or the AMOSPro upgrade, or
AMOSPro V2.... these programs are out of stock, and so it's really hard find
them
somewhere. The programs are commercial and copyrighted, and so YOU CAN'T SPREAD
THEM!!!

Please be patient, as stated in a previous message, in December i'll release
the complete AMOSPro+Compiler package for *FREE DOWNLOAD* on the AMOS Factory
site. Ah... the AMOS Factory site if _#THE OFFICIAL AMOS SITE#_, the url is:

http://www.seta.it/amos/

put it in your browser's bookmark.

Some details about the upgrade. The difference between your AMOSPro copy and
the mine released in december is just some bugs fixes. The MAIN Amospro core
will not be updated... why?

There is a reason.... too many years are elapsed since the last AMOS update..
the today hardware, software and OS situation is totally different. Now gfx
cards and so retargetable gfx and audio, PPC, AGA and so on are a reality, and
the internal AMOS structure is not ready for this. Everything is based on the
old Amiga500 system....the direct hardware access, the OS support and
integration, the programming style etc...... upgrade AMOS with the actual
standards mean TOTALLY rewrite it!!! I'm not so stupid to spend so many time
when between 1 year a totally new amiga will be available!

The AGA support.... add it should be possible but.... the problem is the
compatibility! If we rewrite AMOS and the amos.library with AGA support, all
your previous programs and expecially your extensions will never works
again! I don't think that broke the backward compatibility is a good idea now.

But fortunately AMOS is modular, and so instead of rewrite it we can
add/replace new
functions trough extensions. For this reason i've contacted the best
pd/shareware extensions coders and created the Amos Development Group. We've
joined our efforts, and we'll release our works together as a REAL upgrade.
Thanks to our extensions you'll obtain:

- AGA and gfx cards support
- intuition and gadtools support
- boopsi
- datatypes
- locale
- CDDA
- fast gfx commands great for games coders
- 100% AmigaOS support
- database support

and many, many other cool stuffs.

Hi Everybody,

> Here goes the problem:...
> My game currently features 1 frog/player , I'm gonna copy and
paste
> the code and change the variables name so to have 4
> frogs/players.

Nop, you don't want to do that. It would be too mesy and every time
you wanted to change the game engine you'd have to change 4 things at
once.

I think you should change all the player variebles to arrays :


dim x(3),y(3) etc.

and then put all the players code into a for...next loop:


do

for p=0 to 3

if jleft(1) then x(p)=x(p)-1

bob p+1,x(p),y(p),p+3

etc etc.

next

wait vbl

loop

this would be /slightly/ slower, but its much easier to develop.


> Problem is that the speed is not holding.

Heres what you do:

Timer=0

do

T=Timer
Timer=0

For a=1 to T
----
---- Program code
----
next

----
---- Screen update code.
----

loop



That should make sure that the game runs at roughly the right speed.

I know a lot of people say its a bad idea reseting the timer, but I've
had no problems with it.

	Message #1478 of 8205

Re: Optimizing

Thu Oct 22, 1998 11:03 am
"David Vivash" <PMA98DAV@Sheffield.ac.uk>


> From: erico@www.tecnopro.com.br
>
> Like you said...
>
> > Have you tryed 'AMOSOptimizer.amos' ?
> > If not I can send you a copy of the latest version.
>
> Nice! I haven't tried (nor heard)
> My amos is the 1.3 (that came wirth cu amiga) , will it work?
> please please send to erico@www.tecnopro.com.br
>
> Thanks Peter!
> -----------------------------------------------------------

If you've only got the original AMOS then you could try and get hold
of AMOSPro as this is faster. Also, extensions like the Turbo
extensions will speed up your code.

You said your code is modular - does that mean you call a lot of
procedures? I've found that calling a lot of procedures - especially
from inside your main loop - can slow down your programs.
The amount of optimisation you can do to your code depends on how
optimised it is already. The most basic optimisations come from
changing things like:

A=A+2

to:

Add A,2

(Remember A=A-2 goes to Add A,-2...)
Also A=A+1 can go to Inc A, and A=A-1 goes to Dec A.
Also, if you've got any code like this:

X=X+2 : If X>10 Then X=0
you can change it to Add X,2,0 To 10
This is even more helpful in something like
X=X+A when A can be negative - as your code could look like this:
X=X+A
If X>10 Then X=0
If X<0 Then X=10
This can be changed to just Add X,A,0 To 10
Another point for optimisation is the way you check for joystick
movements. If my memory is right, calling 'If Joy(0)=1...' is quicker
than 'If Jup(0)...' (I can't remember if 1 is up or not though. I
think it's 1=Up, 2=Down, 4=Left, 8=Right, Fire=16 and any composite
direction/fire is just an addition of these, but I'm sure someone
will correct me on these as I haven't got AMOS handy...)
You should also store answers to sums in variables if you use these
answers in more than a few other fuctions.
eg. Add ploy(1,1),16*SCORE-32*(2-LIFE)
Add PLOY(2,1),16*SCORE-32*(2-LIFE)
Add PLOY(3,1),16*SCORE-32*(2-LIFE)
Add PLOY(4,1),16*SCORE-32*(2-LIFE)
should become
X=16*SCORE-32*(2-LIFE)
Add PLOY(1,1),X
Add PLOY(2,1),X etc...

One other little innovation I include in my code (well, an innovation
for me anyway) is that I only update the 'enemies' every certain
number of cycles - and I only update a certain number of those
enemies in any given cycle... That is to say the player never slows
down, but the enemies might sometime. To make things clear, consider
this:

NUM_TO_UPDATE=15
CURRENT=2
MAX_UPDATE=10

For X=1 To 4
Update players...
Next

OKAY=True
A=0
While OKAY=True
..
Update enemy 'CURRENT'
..
Add CURRENT,1,1 To NUM_TO_UPDATE
Inc A
If A=MAXUPDATE Then OKAY = False
Wend

Thus only 10 enemies are updated every cycle (if I've coded it right
which I probably haven't)

Anyway, that's all I can think of for now...

David

	Message #1483 of 8205

Re: Optimizing

Fri Oct 23, 1998 1:04 am
Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>


Hi all,

Here`s my tips on optimising.

1) Use Procedures for your front end/ back end stuff like intros, high
scores etc.
2) Put your main game code up the top in a list of SubRoutines, using
Gosub.
3) Replace for/next loops with repeat/until loops (inc the loop var
yourself)
4) Use INC, DEC and ADD.
5) Process only 1 or 2 aliens per cycle. (this is a great speed
increase) but make sure they still move in other cycles
6) Pop Proc or Return from Procedures / SubRoutines as soon as your code
is done, don`t let it run through all cases unless you need to, and make
each condition modal. ie I have a Range(x,y,mode) proc which tests for
ranges between obj's x and y. mode determines the type of case.

Procedure RANGE(x,y,mode)
if mode=0
...
pop proc
endif
if mode=1
...
pop proc
endif
...
End Proc

7) Use as many colours as you can without a speed loss (and make this
element one of your main focuses for optimisation) because people prefer
more colours and it looks more professional.
8) Process everything thats large in small segements. So if you need to
check the collision between 30 sprites, break it up into 5 sprites per
cycle and check for 6 cycles (at speed this only takes 12vbls - so the
player wont notice). Cue up lower priority tasks when the speed isn`t
important.
Example

Cycle 1 - Process 2 enemy (inc ptr to nxt enemy), Check 5 collisions
Cycle 2 - Update scores, time, check mission status
Cycle 3 - Process 2 enemy (inc ptr to nxt enemy), Check 5 collisions
Cycle 4 - Do nothing
Cycle 5 - Process 2 enemy (inc ptr to nxt enemy), Check 5 collisions
Cycle 6 - Do nothing
Cycle 7 - Process 2 enemy (inc ptr to nxt enemy), Check 5 collisions
Cycle 8 - Set up new enemies, clean up maps etc, normalisation cycle.

Make sure you process the player every cycle though!!!!

9) When using 3d keep the frame rate up, not the number of enemies. 3
well designed enemy ships are harder to kill when the frame rate is
smooth than 10 enemy that just fly in and the frame rate is slow enough
to allow the player to think.

10) When using sprites, keep the number of planes down.
11) When scrolling maps, only paste what the player can see plus a
little off the edges, and when processing enemies off screen give them a
cycle every 2 compared to the ones on the screen.. The player will never
notice.

I guess that`s the thing I found out. When you have a decent frame rate
but the enemy is updated every 2nd or so cycle the player doesn't notice
because the action is speeded up.

Seeya,
Andy H.

	Message #1491 of 8205 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

3-D Optimizing (was 'Optimizing')

Sat Oct 24, 1998 4:50 am
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


>Any more? (especially related to 3D as that's my favorite "toy" right now)

Well, if you're thinking along the lines of Doom or Wolfenstein:
1. Use integers, and nothing else! Be sparing on the Floating Point!
2. It helps to precalculate as much as you can and store it in tables.
3. Peter was right: any type of c2p conversion routines are helpful.
4. It also helps to optimize everything you can in Assembler yourself. :)
5. When writing a Doom-er, KEEP YOUR CODE MODULAR. It's neater that way.

I'm sure these same principles will apply to other types of 3D programs, as
well as a few other genres of games. I may have missed a few, but these
should be enough to get you started (if you weren't aware of any before).

Adam Parrott, mailto: parrotta@usa.net, ICQ# 12967025, Handle: Axianator
The official Parrottsoft site at http://parrottsoft.hypermart.net up soon!

Worlds Fastest C2P's

Fri Oct 23, 1998 5:03 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


Hello!

I remember a few people here mailed me, looking for those
new C2ps that I have They will be put up on my WWW this sunday
so you can download them then, I'll also put the amosOptimizer up
there also. you CAN use these C2Ps from AMOS. Its not hard to do
it wouldn't take more than 5mins to do, all 3D games will benifit
greatly from them, but you can only do 'Plot' to the chunky buffer.
Which you should do like:

Poke C2PBUFFER,C

where C2PBuffer is your place in fastmen that has the c2pbuffer
and 'C' is the colour number. Seen as amos only does
up to 6bitplanes, with the 6bpl version of the c2ps
you'll get about 45FPS at least on the 030.

PS: I'll also be releasing new C2P modules for DoomAttack,
so you'll get to play in fullscreen smoothly!

cyas,

Hello, Everyone..

I've only recived a few bug-reports since I released V3.02 of the AlienBreed
3D-II LevelED 3 months ago. So either there's not many bugs left, or noone
uses the program anymore. Anyway I've decided to release a version that
should fix the few bugs that's been reported. As it seems like the interest
for the editor is dropping I've decided to close the project for now, but
if I might reopen it later on if the interest is present..

As usualy the editor can be downloaded from my homepages, and it should
be availeble on the AmiNET in the near future (circle time)...

NEWS in V3.03 (Released: 25-10-1998)

- More bug-fixes..
- It appears that the interest for the editor is dropping so this might
end up as the last version :-(..

- 'Add objects' would crash when entering values directly..
- 'Define Objects frames' had some old left-overs included..
- 'Define Bullets' also had some old left-overs there..

- Now compiled with amos.library V2.21

Re: Replies for all :)

Sun Oct 25, 1998 9:50 am
Jens Vang Petersen <top_cat@post8.tele.dk>


Hello Peter

On 21-Okt-98, Peter Cahill smashed the keyboard with:
> Ive noticed the Screens in amos2.21 work 100% no errors, well done 8o)
> but is there any chance of you fixing the Do&loop bug ?
>
> It goes like this:
> after a LOT of loops it just hangs and the screen distorts.
> It normally only happens on 030+ as other cpus never do enough
> loops to cause a crash ;)

Normaly this problem shows up when doing very fast loops like:
Do
W$=Inkey$
If W$="".....
Loop

Put a 'Multi Wait' inside the loop and it won't happen..

	Message #1533 of 8212 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

optimization

Wed Oct 28, 1998 8:54 am
"floquet" <floquet@hp-sc.univ-lille2.fr>


Hello, all !

Here is another tip to speed up yous progs:

Repeat
Add x,Jleft(1)
Add x,-Jright(1)
Add y,Jup(1)
Add y,-Jdown(1)
Bob 1,x,y,1
Until fire(1)

It is a VERY useful lack in all Basics, the "logical" type does not
exist, booleans are in fact integers, so you can use them !

In the same way, if "Wmove" is a 0/1 flag, you can replace:
If Wmove = 1
Inc X
End If

with :
Add x,Wmove

I started to use this tip on my ooooold Sinclair ZX81, where speed and
byte-savig were absolutely needed. 1024 bytes of total memory is short !

--
 +____________        +____
 /____   ____/\       /   /
 \___/  __/\_\/ *____/   / AMIGA

	Message #1540 of 8212 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Arexx again....

Thu Oct 29, 1998 8:20 am
"Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>


John,
You could try the Exec function within your AMOS program to execute an
Arexx command or script. The following is a command line I use in one of my
programs, Midi Companion, which addresses the OctaMED Arexx port and sends a
command to turn Midi Active on.

Exec "RX "+chr$(34)+"address octamed_rexx op_set midiactive on"+chr$(34)

It can slow down your program but if you make RX resident it does speed up a
bit.

I tried LDOS which would be great if I could only get it to work properly. I
couldn't get LDOS to recognise the OctaMED Arexx port. LDOS has some good
Arexx commands and if you haven't tried it out yet, you should. It might
just work for you.

Declan.

screenwidth to be a multiple of 16, I now get

97, 125 uncompiled
77, 6 compiled

	Message #1545 of 8212 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: optimization

Fri Oct 30, 1998 2:26 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,


> Here is another tip to speed up yous progs:

> Repeat
> Add x,Jleft(1)
> Add x,-Jright(1)
> Add y,Jup(1)
> Add y,-Jdown(1)
> Bob 1,x,y,1
> Until fire(1)

> It is a VERY useful lack in all Basics, the "logical" type does not
> exist, booleans are in fact integers, so you can use them !

Well, doing thats all well and good if your only moving a simple
opject, but it doesn't allow for propper anims and block collisions.


Any anyway, with the joystick rouines they'll only be called once in
a vbl, so speed isn't /that/ important. Also adding support for
different control setups isn't easy like that either.


I use this method:

---------------------------------------------------------------

cont=0 :Rem Type of controls eg. 0 is joystic 1, 1 is joystic 2.
frm=1

do

gosub chkcont


if l
frm=1 : x=x-1
end if
if r
frm=2 : x=x+1
end if
if u
frm=3 : y=y-1
end if
if d
frm=4 : y=y+1
end if

if f
exit
end if

Bob 1,x,y,frm

wait vbl

loop


chkcont:
if cont=0
if jleft(0)
l=-1
else
l=0
end if
if jright(0)
r=-1
else
r=0
end if
if jup(0)
u=-1
else
u=0
end if
if jdown(0)
d=-1
else
d=0
end if
if fire(0)
f=-1
else
f=0
end if
return
end if

if cont=1
if jleft(1)
l=-1
else
l=0
end if
if jright(1)
r=-1
else
r=0
end if
if jup(1)
u=-1
else
u=0
end if
if jdown(1)
d=-1
else
d=0
end if
if fire(0)
f=-1
else
f=0
end if
return
end if

return

---------------------------------------------------------------


I know its not the fastest, but its modular, easy to use and easy to
add different control configs.


See ya.
